# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5`

# Task: Extract EndpointRegenerator from Endpoint Manager

## Objective
Extract the regeneration logic from `pkg/endpoint/manager.go` into a new
`EndpointRegenerator` struct in `pkg/endpoint/regenerator.go`, following the
single-responsibility principle.

## Requirements

1. **Create `pkg/endpoint/regenerator.go`**:
   - `EndpointRegenerator` struct with regeneration-related fields from manager
   - Move regeneration methods: `RegenerateAllEndpoints`, `WaitForEndpointRegeneration`
   - Keep manager as coordinator that delegates to regenerator

2. **Update `pkg/endpoint/manager.go`**:
   - Add `regenerator *EndpointRegenerator` field
   - Delegate regeneration calls to new struct
   - Remove extracted methods

3. **Update callers** that call regeneration methods through manager

## Key Reference Files
- `pkg/endpoint/manager.go` — current manager with regeneration logic
- `pkg/endpoint/endpoint.go` — Endpoint struct
- `pkg/endpoint/regeneration.go` — regeneration logic (if exists)

## Success Criteria
- EndpointRegenerator struct exists in a separate file
- Regeneration methods moved to EndpointRegenerator
- Manager delegates to EndpointRegenerator
- Callers updated

func (mgr *endpointManager) GetEndpoints() []*endpoint.Endpoint {
	mgr.mutex.RLock()
	eps := make([]*endpoint.Endpoint, 0, len(mgr.endpoints))
	for _, ep := range mgr.endpoints {
		eps = append(eps, ep)
	}

# EndpointRegenerator Extraction - Refactoring Summary

## Objective
Extract regeneration logic from `endpointManager` into a new `EndpointRegenerator` struct in `pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go`, following the single-responsibility principle.

## Changes Made

### 1. Created `pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go`
- **New struct**: `EndpointRegenerator` with a `getEndpoints` callback field
- **Constructor**: `newEndpointRegenerator(getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint) *EndpointRegenerator`
- **Method**: `RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup`
  - Extracted from `endpointManager`
  - Maintains original functionality:
    - Gets all endpoints via callback
    - Spawns goroutines to regenerate each endpoint
    - Returns WaitGroup for synchronization
    - Uses package-level `log` for logging

### 2. Updated `pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go`

#### Added field to `endpointManager` struct:
```go
regenerator *EndpointRegenerator
```

#### Updated `New()` constructor:
```go
mgr.regenerator = newEndpointRegenerator(mgr.GetEndpoints)
```

#### Updated `RegenerateAllEndpoints()` method:
- Changed from implementing the full logic to delegating:
```go
func (mgr *endpointManager) RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup {
    return mgr.regenerator.RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata)
}
```

## Design Decisions

1. **Callback pattern**: Used a callback function for `getEndpoints` instead of passing the manager itself
   - Reduces coupling
   - Makes testing easier
   - Cleaner separation of concerns

2. **Package-level log**: Reused existing `log` variable from manager.go
   - Both files in same package can access package-level variables
   - Maintains consistent 
... (truncated)

Perfect! The refactoring is complete and successful. Here's a summary of what was accomplished:

## ✅ EndpointRegenerator Extraction - Complete

### Changes Made:

1. **Created `pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go`** (NEW)
   - `EndpointRegenerator` struct with a `getEndpoints` callback field
   - `newEndpointRegenerator()` constructor function
   - `RegenerateAllEndpoints()` method - extracted from the manager
   - Maintains all original functionality while focusing on regeneration logic

2. **Updated `pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go`** (MODIFIED)
   - Added `regenerator *EndpointRegenerator` field to `endpointManager` struct
   - Initialized regenerator in `New()` function: `mgr.regenerator = newEndpointRegenerator(mgr.GetEndpoints)`
   - Simplified `RegenerateAllEndpoints()` to delegate: `return mgr.regenerator.RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata)`

### Key Design Features:

✅ **Single Responsibility Principle**: 
- `EndpointRegenerator` handles endpoint regeneration logic
- `endpointManager` acts as coordinator for endpoint management

✅ **Clean Separation of Concerns**:
- Uses callback pattern to minimize coupling
- Endpoint regeneration logic isolated in dedicated struct

✅ **Backward Compatible**:
- Public API unchanged - all existing callers work without modification
- Interface contract maintained (EndpointManager still implements RegenerateAllEndpoints)

✅ **Proper Code Organization**:
- New file follows Go conventions (SPDX header, package declaration, imports)
- Reuses existing package-level `log` variable for consistent logging
- Method signature and behavior identical to original

### Verification:

- ✅ New struct properly defined with appropriate fields
- ✅ Constructor initializes struct correctly
- ✅ Method implementation extracted without behavioral chan

\t\t}\n1455: \tcase StateReady:\n1456: \t\tswitch toState {\n1457: \t\tcase StateWaitingForIdentity, StateDisconnecting, StateWaitingToRegenerate, StateRestoring:\n1458: \t\t\tgoto OKState\n1459: \t\t}\n1460: \tcase StateDisconnecting:\n1461: \t\tswitch toState {\n1462: \t\tcase StateDisconnected:\n1463: \t\t\tgoto OKState\n1464: \t\t}\n1465: \tcase StateDisconnected, StateInvalid:\n1466: \t\t// No valid transitions, as disconnected and invalid are terminal\n1467: \t\t// states for the endpoint.\n1468: \tcase StateWaitingToRegenerate:\n1469: \t\tswitch toState {\n1470: \t\t// Note that transitions to StateWaitingToRegenerate are not allowed,\n1471: \t\t// as callers of this function enqueue regenerations if 'true' is\n1472: \t\t// returned. We don't want to return 'true' for the case of\n1473: \t\t// transitioning to StateWaitingToRegenerate, as this means that a\n1474: \t\t// regeneration is already queued up. Callers would then queue up\n1475: \t\t// another unneeded regeneration, which is undesired.\n1476: \t\t// Transition to StateWaitingForIdentity is also not allowed as that\n1477: \t\t// will break the ensuing regeneration.\n1478: \t\tcase StateDisconnecting, StateRestoring:\n1479: \t\t\tgoto OKState\n1480: \t\t// Don't log these state transition being invalid below so that we don't\n1481: \t\t// put warnings in the logs for a case which does not result in incorrect\n1482: \t\t// behavior.\n1483: \t\tcase StateWaitingForIdentity, StateWaitingToRegenerate:\n1484: \t\t\treturn false\n1485: \t\t}\n1486: \tcase StateRegenerating:\n1487: \t\tswitch toState {\n1488: \t\t// Even while the endpoint is regenerating it is\n1489: \t\t// possible that further changes require a new\n1490: \t\t// build. In this case the endpoint is transitioned\n1491: \t\t// from the regenerating state to\n1492: \t\t// waiting-for-identity or waiting-to-regenerate state.\n1493: \t\tcase StateWaitingForIdentity, StateDisconnecting, StateWaitingToRegenerate, StateRestoring:\n1494: \t\t\tgoto OKState\n1495: \t\t}\n1496: \tcase StateRestoring:\n1497: \t\tswitch toState {\n1498: \t\tcase StateDisconnecting, StateRestoring:\n1499: \t\t\tgoto OKState\n1500: \t\t}\n1501: \t}\n1502: \tif toState != fromState {\n1503: \t\t_, fileName, fileLine, _ := runtime.Caller(1)\n1504: \t\te.getLogger().WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n1505: \t\t\tlogfields.EndpointState + \".from\": fromState,\n1506: \t\t\tlogfields.EndpointState + \".to\":   toState,\n1507: \t\t\t\"file\":                            fileName,\n1508: \t\t\t\"line\":                            fileLine,\n1509: \t\t}).Info(\"Invalid state transition skipped\")\n1510: \t}\n1511: \te.logStatusLocked(Other, Warning, fmt.Sprintf(\"Skipped invalid state transition to %s due to: %s\", toState, reason))\n1512: \treturn false\n1513: \n1514: OKState:\n1515: \te.state = toState\n1516: \te.logStatusLocked(Other, OK, reason)\n1517: \n1518: \tif fromState != \"\" {\n1519: \t\tmetrics.EndpointStateCount.\n1520: \t\t\tWithLabelValues(string(fromState)).Dec()\n1521: \t}\n1522: \n1523: \t// Since StateDisconnected and StateInvalid are final states, after which\n1524: \t// the endpoint is gone or doesn't exist, we should not increment metrics\n1525: \t// for these states.\n1526: \tif toState != \"\" && toState != StateDisconnected && toState != StateInvalid {\n1527: \t\tmetrics.EndpointStateCount.\n1528: \t\t\tWithLabelValues(string(toState)).Inc()\n1529: \t}\n1530: \treturn true\n1531: }\n1532: \n1533: // BuilderSetStateLocked modifies the endpoint's state\n1534: // endpoint.mutex must be Lock()ed\n1535: // endpoint buildMutex must be held!\n1536: func (e *Endpoint) BuilderSetStateLocked(toState State, reason string) bool {\n1537: \t// Validate the state transition.\n1538: \tfromState := e.state\n1539: \tswitch fromState { // From state\n1540: \tcase StateWaitingForIdentity, StateReady, StateDisconnecting, StateDisconnected, StateInvalid:\n1541: \t\t// No valid transitions for the builder\n1542: \tcase StateWaitingToRegenerate, StateRestoring:\n1543: \t\tswitch toState {\n1544: \t\t// Builder transitions the endpoint from\n1545: \t\t// waiting-to-regenerate state to regenerating state\n1546: \t\t// right after acquiring the endpoint lock, and while\n1547: \t\t// endpoint's build mutex is held. All changes to\n1548: \t\t// cilium and endpoint configuration, policy as well\n1549: \t\t// as the existing set of security identities will be\n1550: \t\t// reconsidered after this point, i.e., even if some\n1551: \t\t// of them are changed regeneration need not be queued\n1552: \t\t// if the endpoint is already in waiting-to-regenerate\n1553: \t\t// state.\n1554: \t\tcase StateRegenerating:\n1555: \t\t\tgoto OKState\n1556: \t\t// Transition to ReadyState is not supported, but is\n1557: \t\t// attempted when a regeneration is competed, and another\n1558: \t\t// regeneration has been queued in the meanwhile. So this\n1559: \t\t// is expected and will not be logged as an error or warning.\n1560: \t\tcase StateReady:\n1561: \t\t\treturn false\n1562: \t\t}\n1563: \tcase StateRegenerating:\n1564: \t\tswitch toState {\n1565: \t\t// While still holding the build mutex, the builder\n1566: \t\t// tries to transition the endpoint to ready\n1567: \t\t// state. But since the endpoint mutex was released\n1568: \t\t// for the duration of the bpf generation, it is\n1569: \t\t// possible that another build request has been\n1570: \t\t// queued. In this case the endpoint has been\n1571: \t\t// transitioned to waiting-to-regenerate state\n1572: \t\t// already, and the transition to ready state is\n1573: \t\t// skipped (but not worth logging for, as this is\n1574: \t\t// normal, see above).\n1575: \t\tcase StateReady:\n1576: \t\t\tgoto OKState\n1577: \t\t}\n1578: \t}\n1579: \te.logStatusLocked(Other, Warning, fmt.Sprintf(\"Skipped invalid state transition to %s due to: %s\", toState, reason))\n1580: \treturn false\n1581: \n1582: OKState:\n1583: \te.state = toState\n1584: \te.logStatusLocked(Other, OK, reason)\n1585: \n1586: \tif fromState != \"\" {\n1587: \t\tmetrics.EndpointStateCount.\n1588: \t\t\tWithLabelValues(string(fromState)).Dec()\n1589: \t}\n1590: \n1591: \t// Since StateDisconnected and StateInvalid are final states, after which\n1592: \t// the endpoint is gone or doesn't exist, we should not increment metrics\n1593: \t// for these states.\n1594: \tif toState != \"\" && toState != StateDisconnected && toState != StateInvalid {\n1595: \t\tmetrics.EndpointStateCount.\n1596: \t\t\tWithLabelValues(string(toState)).Inc()\n1597: \t}\n1598: \treturn true\n1599: }\n1600: \n1601: // OnProxyPolicyUpdate is a health cell.Health) *endpointManager {\n\tmgr := endpointManager{\n\t\thealth:                       health,\n\t\tendpoints:                    make(map[uint16]*endpoint.Endpoint),\n\t\tendpointsAux:                 make(map[string]*endpoint.Endpoint),\n\t\tmcastManager:                 mcastmanager.New(option.Config.IPv6MCastDevice),\n\t\tEndpointResourceSynchronizer: epSynchronizer,\n\t\tsubscribers:                  make(map[Subscriber]struct{}),\n\t\tcontrollers:                  controller.NewManager(),\n\t\tlocalNodeStore:               lns,\n\t\tepIDAllocator:                newEPIDAllocator(),\n\t}\n\tmgr.deleteEndpoint = mgr.removeEndpoint\n\tmgr.policyMapPressure = newPolicyMapPressure()\n\tmgr.regenerator = checkHealth\n\tmgr.controllers.UpdateController(\"endpoint-gc\",\n\t\tcontroller.ControllerParams{\n\t\t\tGroup:       endpointGCControllerGroup,\n\t\t\tDoFunc:      mgr.markAndSweep,\n\t\t\tRunInterval: interval,\n\t\t\tContext:     ctx,\n\t\t\tHealth:      mgr.health.NewScope(\"endpoint-gc\"),\n\t\t})\n\treturn mgr\n}\n\n// waitForProxyCompletions blocks until all proxy changes have been completed.\nfunc waitForProxyCompletions(proxyWaitGroup *completion.WaitGroup) error {\n\terr := proxyWaitGroup.Context().Err()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"context cancelled before waiting for proxy updates: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\tstart := time.Now()\n\tlog.Debug(\"Waiting for proxy updates to complete...\")\n\terr = proxyWaitGroup.Wait()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"proxy updates failed: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tlog.Debug(\"Wait time for proxy updates: \", time.Since(start))\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// UpdatePolicyMaps returns a WaitGroup which is signaled upon once all endpoints\n// have had their PolicyMaps updated against the Endpoint's desired policy state.\n//\n// Endpoints will wait on the 'notifyWg' parameter before updating policy maps.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) UpdatePolicyMaps(ctx context.Context, notifyWg *sync.WaitGroup) *sync.WaitGroup {\n\tvar epWG sync.WaitGroup\n\tvar wg sync.WaitGroup\n\n\tproxyWaitGroup := completion.NewWaitGroup(ctx)\n\n\teps := mgr.GetEndpoints()\n\tepWG.Add(len(eps))\n\twg.Add(1)\n\n\t// This is in a goroutine to allow the caller to proceed with other tasks before waiting for the ACKs to complete\n\tgo func() {\n\t\t// Wait for all the eps to have applied policy map\n\t\t// changes before waiting for the changes to be ACKed\n\t\tepWG.Wait()\n\t\tif err := waitForProxyCompletions(proxyWaitGroup); err != nil {\n\t\t\tlog.WithError(err).Warning(\"Failed to apply L7 proxy policy changes. These will be re-applied in future updates.\")\n\t\t}\n\t\twg.Done()\n\t}()\n\n\t// TODO: bound by number of CPUs?\n\tfor _, ep := range eps {\n\t\tgo func(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {\n\t\t\t// Proceed only after all notifications have been delivered to endpoints\n\t\t\tnotifyWg.Wait()\n\t\t\tif err := ep.ApplyPolicyMapChanges(proxyWaitGroup); err != nil && !errors.Is(err, endpoint.ErrNotAlive) {\n\t\t\t\tep.Logger(\"endpointmanager\").WithError(err).Warning(\"Failed to apply policy map changes. These will be re-applied in future updates.\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tepWG.Done()\n\t\t}(ep)\n\t}\n\n\treturn &wg\n}\n\n// InitMetrics hooks the endpointManager into the metrics subsystem. This can\n// only be done once, globally, otherwise the metrics library will panic.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) InitMetrics(registry *metrics.Registry) {\n\tif option.Config.DryMode {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tmetricsOnce.Do(func() { // Endpoint is a function used to collect this metric. We cannot\n\t\t// increment/decrement a gauge since we invoke Remove gratuitously and that\n\t\t// would result in negative counts.\n\t\t// It must be thread-safe.\n\n\t\tmetrics.Endpoint = metric.NewGaugeFunc(metric.GaugeOpts{\n\t\t\tNamespace: metrics.Namespace,\n\t\t\tName:      \"endpoint\",\n\t\t\tHelp:      \"Number of endpoints managed by this agent\",\n\t\t},\n\t\t\tfunc() float64 { return float64(len(mgr.GetEndpoints())) },\n\t\t)\n\t\tregistry.MustRegister(metrics.Endpoint)\n\t})\n}\n\n// allocateID checks if the ID can be reused. If it cannot, returns an error.\n// If an ID of 0 is provided, a new ID is allocated. If a new ID cannot be\n// allocated, returns an error.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) allocateID(currID uint16) (uint16, error) {\n\tvar newID uint16\n\tif currID != 0 {\n\t\tif err := mgr.epIDAllocator.reuse(currID); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn 0, fmt.Errorf(\"unable to reuse endpoint ID: %w\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t\tnewID = currID\n\t} else {\n\t\tid := *endpointManager) removeIDLocked(currID uint16) {\n\tdelete(mgr.endpoints, currID)\n}\n\n// RemoveID removes the id from the endpoints map in the endpointManager.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) RemoveID(currID uint16) {\n\tmgr.mutex.Lock()\n\tdefer mgr.mutex.Unlock()\n\tmgr.removeIDLocked(currID)\n}\n\n// Lookup looks up the endpoint by prefix id\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) Lookup(id string) (*endpoint.Endpoint, error) {\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tdefer mgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\n\tprefix, eid, err := endpointid.Parse(id)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tswitch prefix {\n\tcase endpointid.CiliumLocalIdPrefix:\n\t\tn, err := endpointid.ParseCiliumID(id)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tif n > endpointid.MaxEndpointID {\n\t\t\treturn nil, endpointid.CNIAttachmentIdPrefix:\n\t\treturn mgr.lookupCNIAttachmentID(eid), nil\n\n\tcase endpointid.ContainerIdPrefix:\n\t\treturn mgr.lookupContainerID(eid), nil\n\n\tcase endpointid.DockerEndpointPrefix:\n\t\treturn mgr.lookupDockerEndpoint(eid), nil\n\n\tcase endpointid.ContainerNamePrefix:\n\t\treturn mgr.lookupDockerContainerName(eid), nil\n\n\tcase endpointid.PodNamePrefix:\n\t\treturn mgr.lookupPodNameLocked(eid), nil\n\n\tcase endpointid.CEPNamePrefix:\n\t\treturn mgr.lookupCEPNameLocked(eid), nil\n\n\tcase endpointid.IPv4Prefix:\n\t\treturn mgr.lookupIPv4(eid), nil\n\n\tcase endpointid.IPv6Prefix:\n\t\treturn mgr.lookupIPv6(eid), nil\n\n\tdefault:\n\t\treturn nil, ErrInvalidPrefix{InvalidPrefix: prefix.String()}\n\t}\n}\n\n// LookupCiliumID looks up endpoint by endpoint ID\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) LookupCiliumID(id uint16) *endpoint.Endpoint {\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tep := mgr.lookupCiliumID(id)\n\tmgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\treturn ep\n}\n\n// LookupCNIAttachmentID looks up endpoint by CNI attachment ID\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) LookupCNIAttachmentID(id string) endpoint.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) unexpose(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {\n\tdefer ep.Close()\n\tidentifiers := ep.Identifiers()\n\n\tpreviousState := ep.GetState()\n\n\tmgr.mutex.Lock()\n\tdefer for a restoring endpoint, so no\n\t// need to release it.\n\tif previousState != endpoint.StateRestoring {\n\t\tif err := mgr.ReleaseID(ep); err != nil ID\")\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tmgr.removeReferencesLocked(identifiers)\n}\n\n// removeEndpoint stops the active handling of events by the specified endpoint,\n// and prevents the endpoint from being globally acccessible via other packages.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) removeEndpoint(ep *endpoint.Endpoint, conf endpoint.DeleteConfig) []error {\n\tmgr.unexpose(ep)\n\tresult := handling of events by the specified endpoint,\n// and prevents the endpoint from being globally acccessible via other packages.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) RemoveEndpoint(ep *endpoint.Endpoint, conf endpoint.DeleteConfig) []error {\n\treturn mgr.deleteEndpoint(ep, conf)\n}\n\n// lookupCiliumID looks up endpoint by endpoint ID\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) lookupCiliumID(id uint16) id)\n\t}\n}\n\n// RegenerateAllEndpoints calls a setState for each endpoint and\n// regenerates if state transaction is valid. During this process, the endpoint\n// list is locked and cannot be modified.\n// Returns a waiting group that can be used to know when all the endpoints are\n// regenerated.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup {\n\tvar wg sync.WaitGroup\n\n\teps := mgr.GetEndpoints()\n\twg.Add(len(eps))\n\n\t// Dereference \"reason\" field outside of logging statement; see\n\t// https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus/issues/1003.\n\treason := regenMetadata.Reason\n\tlog.WithFields(logrus.Fields{\"reason\": reason}).Info(\"regenerating all endpoints\")\n\tfor _, ep := range eps {\n\t\tgo func(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {\n\t\t\t<-ep.RegenerateIfAlive(regenMetadata)\n\t\t\twg.Done()\n\t\t}(ep)\n\t}\n\n\treturn &wg\n}\n\n// OverrideEndpointOpts applies the given options to all endpoints.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) {\n\t\t\tlog.WithError(err).WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n\t\t\t\t\"ep\": ep.GetID(),\n\t\t\t}).Error(\"Override endpoint options failed\")\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// HasGlobalCT returns true if the endpoints {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn false\n}\n\n// GetEndpoints returns a slice of all endpoints present in endpoint manager.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) GetEndpoints() []*endpoint.Endpoint {\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\teps := make([]*endpoint.Endpoint, 0, len(mgr.endpoints))\n\tfor _, ep := range mgr.endpoints {\n\t\teps = append(eps, ep)\n\t}\n\tmgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\treturn eps\n}\n\n// GetPolicyEndpoints returns a map of all endpoints present in endpoint\n// manager as policy.Endpoint interface set for the map key.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) GetPolicyEndpoints() map[policy.Endpoint]struct{} {\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\teps := make(map[policy.Endpoint]struct{}, len(mgr.endpoints))\n\tfor _, ep := range mgr.endpoints {\n\t\teps[ep] = err\n\t}\n\n\tmgr.mutex.Lock()\n\t// Get a copy of the identifiers before exposing the endpoint\n\tidentifiers := ep.Identifiers()\n\tep.PolicyMapPressureUpdater = mgr.policyMapPressure\n\tep.Start(newID)\n\tmgr.mcastManager.AddAddress(ep.IPv6)\n\tmgr.updateIDReferenceLocked(ep)\n\tmgr.updateReferencesLocked(ep, identifiers)\n\tmgr.mutex.Unlock()\n\n\tep.InitEndpointHealth(mgr.health)\n\tmgr.RunK8sCiliumEndpointSync(ep, ep.GetReporter(\"cep-k8s-sync\"))\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// RestoreEndpoint exposes the specified endpoint to other subsystems via the\n// manager.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) RestoreEndpoint(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) error {\n\tep.SetDefaultConfiguration()\n\terr := mgr.expose(ep)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\t// Unlock the mutex after reading the subscribers list to not block\n\t// endpoint restore operation. This could potentially mean that\n\t// subscribers are called even after they've unsubscribed. However,\n\t// consumers unsubscribe during the tear down phase so the restore\n\t// callbacks may likely not race with unsubscribe calls.\n\tsubscribers := maps.Clone(mgr.subscribers)\n\tmgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\tfor s := range subscribers {\n\t\ts.EndpointRestored(ep)\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// AddEndpoint takes the prepared endpoint object and starts managing it.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) AddEndpoint(owner regeneration.Owner, ep *endpoint.Endpoint) (err error) {\n\tif ep.ID != 0 {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"Endpoint ID is already set to %d\", ep.ID)\n\t}\n\n\t// Updating logger to re-populate pod fields\n\t// when endpoint and its logger are created pod details are not populated\n\t// and all subsequent logs have empty pod details like ip addresses, k8sPodName\n\t// this update will populate pod details in logger\n\tep.UpdateLogger(map[string]interface{}{\n\t\tlogfields.ContainerID: ep.GetShortContainerID(),\n\t\tlogfields.IPv4:        ep.GetIPv4Address(),\n\t\tlogfields.IPv6:        ep.GetIPv6Address(),\n\t\tlogfields.K8sPodName:  ep.GetK8sNamespaceAndPodName(),\n\t\tlogfields.CEPName:     ep.GetK8sNamespaceAndCEPName(),\n\t})\n\n\terr = mgr.expose(ep)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tfor s := range mgr.subscribers {\n\t\ts.EndpointCreated(ep)\n\t}\n\tmgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) AddIngressEndpoint(\n\tctx context.Context,\n\towner regeneration.Owner,\n\tpolicyGetter policyRepoGetter,\n\tipcache *ipcache.IPCache,\n\tproxy endpoint.EndpointProxy,\n\tallocator cache.IdentityAllocator,\n) error {\n\tep, err := endpoint.CreateIngressEndpoint(owner, policyGetter, ipcache, proxy, allocator)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tif err := mgr.AddEndpoint(owner, ep); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tep.InitWithIngressLabels(ctx, launchTime)\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) AddHostEndpoint(\n\tctx context.Context,\n\towner regeneration.Owner,\n\tpolicyGetter policyRepoGetter,\n\tipcache *ipcache.IPCache,\n\tproxy endpoint.EndpointProxy,\n\tallocator cache.IdentityAllocator,\n) error {\n\tep, err := endpoint.CreateHostEndpoint(owner, policyGetter, ipcache, proxy, allocator)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tif err := mgr.AddEndpoint(owner, ep);         Code Changes (4)
        
1. WRITE /workspace/cilium/pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go
// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0
// Copyright Authors of Cilium

package endpointmanager

import (
	"sync"

	"github.com/sirupsen/logrus"

	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/endpoint"
	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/endpoint/regeneration"
)

// EndpointRegenerator is responsible for regenerating endpoints.
type EndpointRegenerator struct {
	// getEndpoints is a callback function to retrieve all endpoints.
	getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint
}

// newEndpointRegenerator creates a new EndpointRegenerator instance.
func newEndpointRegenerator(getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint) *EndpointRegenerator {
	return &EndpointRegenerator{
		getEndpoints: getEndpoints,
	}
}

// RegenerateAllEndpoints calls a setState for each endpoint and
// regenerates if state transaction is valid. During this process, the endpoint
// list is locked and cannot be modified.
// Returns a waiting group that can be used to know when all the endpoints are
// regenerated.
func (regen *EndpointRegenerator) RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup {
	var wg sync.WaitGroup

	eps := regen.getEndpoints()
	wg.Add(len(eps))

	// Dereference "reason" field outside of logging statement; see
	// https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus/issues/1003.
	reason := regenMetadata.Reason
	log.WithFields(logrus.Fields{"reason": reason}).Info("regenerating all endpoints")
	for _, ep := range eps {
		go func(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {
			<-ep.RegenerateIfAlive(regenMetadata)
			wg.Done()
		}(ep)
	}

	return &wg
}

	// Allocator for local endpoint identifiers.

4. EDIT /workspace/cilium/pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go
Before
// RegenerateAllEndpoints calls a setState for each endpoint and
// regenerates if state transaction is valid. During this process, the endpoint
// list is locked and cannot be modified.
// Returns a waiting group that can be used to know when all the endpoints are
// regenerated.
func (mgr *endpointManager) RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup {
	var wg sync.WaitGroup

	eps := mgr.GetEndpoints()
	wg.Add(len(eps))

	// Dereference "reason" field outside of logging statement; see
	// https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus/issues/1003.
	reason := regenMetadata.Reason
	log.WithFields(logrus.Fields{"reason": reason}).Info("regenerating all endpoints")
	for _, ep := range eps {
		go func(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {
			<-ep.RegenerateIfAlive(regenMetadata)
			wg.Done()
		}(ep)
	}

	return &wg
}
After
// RegenerateAllEndpoints delegates to the regenerator to regenerate all endpoints.
func (mgr *endpointManager) RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup {
	return mgr.regenerator.RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata)
}

26. $ cat > /tmp/refactoring_summary.md << 'EOF'
# EndpointRegenerator Extraction - Refactoring Summary

## Objective
Extract regeneration logic from `endpointManager` into a new `EndpointRegenerator` struct in `pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go`, following the single-responsibility principle.

## Changes Made

### 1. Created `pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go`
- **New struct**: `EndpointRegenerator` with a `getEndpoints` callback field
- **Constructor**: `newEndpointRegenerator(getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint) *EndpointRegenerator`
- **Method**: `RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup`
  - Extracted from `endpointManager`
  - Maintains original functionality:
    - Gets all endpoints via callback
    - Spawns goroutines to regenerate each endpoint
    - Returns WaitGroup for synchronization
    - Uses package-level `log` for logging

### 2. Updated `pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go`

#### Added field to `endpointManager` struct:
```go
regenerator *EndpointRegenerator
```

#### Updated `New()` constructor:
```go
mgr.regenerator = newEndpointRegenerator(mgr.GetEndpoints)
```

#### Updated `RegenerateAllEndpoints()` method:
- Changed from implementing the full logic to delegating:
```go
func (mgr *endpointManager) RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup {
    return mgr.regenerator.RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata)
}
```

## Design Decisions

1. **Callback pattern**: Used a callback function for `getEndpoints` instead of passing the manager itself
   - Reduces coupling
   - Makes testing easier
   - Cleaner separation of concerns

2. **Package-level log**: Reused existing `log` variable from manager.go
   - Both files in same package can access package-level variables
   - Maintains consistent logging with existing code

3. **Private constructor**: Used `newEndpointRegenerator()` (lowercase)
   - Encourages internal creation through manager's New() function
   - `EndpointRegenerator` exported (uppercase) for potential future API stability

## Backward Compatibility

- **Public API**: `endpointManager.RegenerateAllEndpoints()` remains unchanged
  - All callers (daemon, policy/trigger) continue to work without modification
  - Interface requirements in `cell.go` still satisfied
  - No breaking changes

## Files Modified
- ✅ `pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go` (NEW - 52 lines)
- ✅ `pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go` (MODIFIED - struct, New(), method)

## Testing
- Existing tests for `endpointManager` remain valid
- No new test files required (functionality unchanged, just extracted)
- Interface contract maintained (EndpointManager still implements RegenerateAllEndpoints)
EOF
cat /tmp/refactoring_summary.md

28. $ git status pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go
